A <a href="/wiki/Nissan_Leaf" title="Nissan Leaf">Nissan Leaf</a> <a href="/wiki/Electric_car" title="Electric car">electric car</a> recharging at an on-street public charging station in <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a></div>
</div>

<p>An <b>electric vehicle</b> (<b>EV</b>), also referred to as an <b>electric drive vehicle</b>, uses one or more <a href="/wiki/Electric_motor" title="Electric motor">electric motors</a> or <a href="/wiki/Traction_motor" title="Traction motor">traction motors</a> for <a href="/wiki/Ground_propulsion" title="Ground propulsion">propulsion</a>. Three main types of electric <a href="/wiki/Vehicle" title="Vehicle">vehicles</a> exist, those that are directly powered from an external power station, those that are powered by stored electricity originally from an external power source, and those that are powered by an on-board electrical generator, such as an internal combustion engine (a hybrid electric vehicle) or a hydrogen fuel cell.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup> EVs include <a href="/wiki/Electric_car" title="Electric car">electric cars</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electric_train" title="Electric train">electric trains</a>, electric lorries, <a href="/wiki/Electric_airplane" title="Electric airplane" class="mw-redirect">electric aeroplanes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electric_boat" title="Electric boat">electric boats</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electric_motorcycles_and_scooters" title="Electric motorcycles and scooters">electric motorcycles and scooters</a> and <a href="/wiki/Electrically_powered_spacecraft_propulsion" title="Electrically powered spacecraft propulsion">electric spacecraft</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> Diesel submarines operating on battery power are, for the duration of the battery run, electric submarines, and some of the lighter <a href="/wiki/UAV" title="UAV" class="mw-redirect">UAVs</a> are electrically-powered. Proposals exist for <a href="/wiki/Altay_(tank)" title="Altay (tank)">electric tanks</a>.</p>
<p>EVs first came into existence in the mid-19th century, when electricity was among the preferred methods for motor vehicle propulsion, providing a level of comfort and ease of operation that could not be achieved by the gasoline cars of the time. The <a href="/wiki/Internal_combustion_engine" title="Internal combustion engine">internal combustion engine</a> (ICE) is the dominant propulsion method for <a href="/wiki/Automobile" title="Automobile">motor vehicles</a> but electric power has remained commonplace in other vehicle types, such as trains and smaller vehicles of all types.</p>
<p>During the last few decades, <a href="/wiki/Environmental_issues_with_petroleum" title="Environmental issues with petroleum" class="mw-redirect">environmental impact</a> of the petroleum-based transportation infrastructure, along with the <a href="/wiki/Peak_oil" title="Peak oil">peak oil</a>, has led to renewed interest in an electric transportation infrastructure.<sup id="cite_ref-RSC_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RSC-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> EVs differ from <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel" title="Fossil fuel">fossil fuel</a>-powered vehicles in that the electricity they consume can be generated from a wide range of sources, including fossil fuels, <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power" title="Nuclear power">nuclear power</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy" title="Renewable energy">renewable</a> sources such as <a href="/wiki/Tidal_power" title="Tidal power">tidal power</a>, <a href="/wiki/Solar_power" title="Solar power">solar power</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wind_power" title="Wind power">wind power</a> or any combination of those. Currently, though, there are more than 400 coal power plants in the U.S. alone,<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> meaning that EV operation in regions serviced by these plants are effectively burning coal for locomotion. However it is generated, this energy is then transmitted to the vehicle through use of <a href="/wiki/Overhead_lines" title="Overhead lines" class="mw-redirect">overhead lines</a>, which necessarily involves transmission loss, <a href="/wiki/Wireless_energy_transfer" title="Wireless energy transfer" class="mw-redirect">wireless energy transfer</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Inductive_charging" title="Inductive charging">inductive charging</a>, or a direct connection through an electrical cable. The electricity may then be stored on board the vehicle using a <a href="/wiki/Battery_(electricity)" title="Battery (electricity)">battery</a>, <a href="/wiki/Flywheel_energy_storage" title="Flywheel energy storage">flywheel</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Supercapacitor" title="Supercapacitor">supercapacitors</a>. Vehicles making use of engines working on the principle of <a href="/wiki/Internal_combustion_engine" title="Internal combustion engine">combustion</a> can usually only derive their energy from a single or a few sources, usually non-renewable fossil fuels. A key advantage of electric or hybrid EVs is <a href="/wiki/Regenerative_braking" title="Regenerative braking" class="mw-redirect">regenerative braking</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shock_absorber" title="Shock absorber">suspension</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> their ability to recover energy normally lost during braking as electricity to be restored to the on-board battery or to the <a href="/wiki/Electrical_grid" title="Electrical grid">electrical grid</a>.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_electric_vehicle" title="History of the electric vehicle">History of the electric vehicle</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jedlik%27s_electric-car.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Jedlik%27s_electric-car.PNG/220px-Jedlik%27s_electric-car.PNG" width="220" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Jedlik%27s_electric-car.PNG/330px-Jedlik%27s_electric-car.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/39/Jedlik%27s_electric-car.PNG 2x" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jedlik%27s_electric-car.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf13/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>
EV model by <a href="/wiki/%C3%81nyos_Jedlik" title="Ányos Jedlik">Ányos Jedlik</a>, an early <a href="/wiki/Electric_motor" title="Electric motor">electric motor</a> experimenter (1828, Hungary)</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:EdisonElectricCar1913.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/EdisonElectricCar1913.jpg/220px-EdisonElectricCar1913.jpg" width="220" height="174" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/EdisonElectricCar1913.jpg/330px-EdisonElectricCar1913.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/EdisonElectricCar1913.jpg/440px-EdisonElectricCar1913.jpg 2x" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:EdisonElectricCar1913.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf13/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Thomas_Edison" title="Thomas Edison">Edison</a> and a 1914 <a href="/wiki/Detroit_Electric" title="Detroit Electric">Detroit Electric</a>, model 47 (courtesy of the <a href="/wiki/National_Museum_of_American_History" title="National Museum of American History">National Museum of American History</a>)</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Electric_car_and_antique_car_on_display_at_1912_auto_show.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Electric_car_and_antique_car_on_display_at_1912_auto_show.jpg/220px-Electric_car_and_antique_car_on_display_at_1912_auto_show.jpg" width="220" height="125" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Electric_car_and_antique_car_on_display_at_1912_auto_show.jpg/330px-Electric_car_and_antique_car_on_display_at_1912_auto_show.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Electric_car_and_antique_car_on_display_at_1912_auto_show.jpg/440px-Electric_car_and_antique_car_on_display_at_1912_auto_show.jpg 2x" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Electric_car_and_antique_car_on_display_at_1912_auto_show.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf13/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>
An EV and an antique car on display at a 1912 auto show</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Electric motive power started with a small drifter operated by a miniature electric motor, built by <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Davenport_(inventor)" title="Thomas Davenport (inventor)">Thomas Davenport</a> in 1835. In 1838, a Scotsman named <a href="/wiki/Robert_Davidson_(inventor)" title="Robert Davidson (inventor)">Robert Davidson</a> built an electric locomotive that attained a speed of four miles per hour (6&#160;km/h). In England a patent was granted in 1840 for the use of rails as conductors of electric current, and similar American patents were issued to <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lilley_and_Colten&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Lilley and Colten (page does not exist)">Lilley and Colten</a> in 1847.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Between 1832 and 1839 (the exact year is uncertain), <a href="/wiki/Robert_Anderson_(inventor)" title="Robert Anderson (inventor)">Robert Anderson</a> of <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a> invented the first crude electric carriage, powered by non-rechargeable <a href="/wiki/Primary_cell" title="Primary cell">primary cells</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>By the 20th century, <a href="/wiki/Electric_car" title="Electric car">electric cars</a> and rail transport were commonplace, with commercial electric automobiles having the majority of the market. Over time their general-purpose commercial use reduced to specialist roles, as <a href="/wiki/Electric_platform_truck" title="Electric platform truck">platform trucks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Forklift_truck" title="Forklift truck">forklift trucks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ambulance" title="Ambulance">ambulances</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> tow tractors and urban delivery vehicles, such as the iconic British <a href="/wiki/Milk_float" title="Milk float">milk float</a>; for most of the 20th century, the UK was the world's largest user of electric road vehicles.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Electrified trains were used for <a href="/wiki/Coal" title="Coal">coal</a> transport, as the motors did not use precious <a href="/wiki/Oxygen" title="Oxygen">oxygen</a> in the mines. Switzerland's lack of natural fossil resources forced the rapid electrification of <a href="/wiki/Rail_transport_in_Switzerland" title="Rail transport in Switzerland">their rail network</a>. One of the earliest <a href="/wiki/Rechargeable_batteries" title="Rechargeable batteries" class="mw-redirect">rechargeable batteries</a> - the <a href="/wiki/Nickel-iron_battery" title="Nickel-iron battery" class="mw-redirect">nickel-iron battery</a> - was favored by <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Edison" title="Thomas Edison">Edison</a> for use in <a href="/wiki/Electric_cars" title="Electric cars" class="mw-redirect">electric cars</a>.</p>
<p>EVs were among the earliest automobiles, and before the preeminence of light, powerful <a href="/wiki/Internal_combustion_engines" title="Internal combustion engines" class="mw-redirect">internal combustion engines</a>, electric automobiles held many vehicle land speed and distance records in the early 1900s. They were produced by <a href="/wiki/Baker_Electric" title="Baker Electric" class="mw-redirect">Baker Electric</a>, <a href="/wiki/Columbia_Automobile_Company" title="Columbia Automobile Company">Columbia Electric</a>, <a href="/wiki/Detroit_Electric" title="Detroit Electric">Detroit Electric</a>, and others, and at one point in history out-sold gasoline-powered vehicles. In fact, in 1900, 28 percent of the cars on the road in the USA were electric. EVs were so popular that even President <a href="/wiki/Woodrow_Wilson" title="Woodrow Wilson">Woodrow Wilson</a> and his secret service agents toured Washington DC in their Milburn Electrics, which covered 60–70 miles per charge.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In the 1930s, <a href="/wiki/National_City_Lines" title="National City Lines">National City Lines</a>, which was a partnership of <a href="/wiki/General_Motors" title="General Motors">General Motors</a>, <a href="/wiki/Firestone_Tire_and_Rubber_Company" title="Firestone Tire and Rubber Company">Firestone</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Standard_Oil_of_California" title="Standard Oil of California" class="mw-redirect">Standard Oil of California</a> purchased many electric <a href="/wiki/Tram" title="Tram">tram</a> networks across the country to dismantle them and replace them with GM buses. The partnership was convicted of conspiring to monopolize the sale of equipment and supplies to their subsidiary companies <a href="/wiki/General_Motors_streetcar_conspiracy" title="General Motors streetcar conspiracy">conspiracy</a>, but were acquitted of conspiring to monopolize the provision of transportation services. Electric tram line technologies could be used to recharge <a href="/wiki/Battery_electric_vehicle" title="Battery electric vehicle">BEVs</a> and <a href="/wiki/PHEV" title="PHEV" class="mw-redirect">PHEVs</a> on the highway while the user drives, providing virtually unrestricted driving range. The technology is old and well established (see&#160;: <a href="/wiki/Conduit_current_collection" title="Conduit current collection">Conduit current collection</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nickel-iron_battery" title="Nickel-iron battery" class="mw-redirect">Nickel-iron battery</a>). The infrastructure has not been built.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Experimentation">Experimentation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Experimentation">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Experimentation" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In January 1990, General Motors' President introduced its EV concept two-seater, the "Impact", at the Los Angeles Auto Show. That September, the California Air Resources Board mandated major-automaker sales of EVs, in phases starting in 1998. From 1996 to 1998 GM produced 1117 EV1s, 800 of which were made available through three-year leases.</p>
<p>Chrysler, Ford, GM, Honda, Nissan and Toyota also produced limited numbers of EVs for California drivers. In 2003, upon the expiration of GM's <a href="/wiki/General_Motors_EV1" title="General Motors EV1">EV1</a> leases, GM crushed them. The crushing has variously been attributed to 1) the auto industry's successful <a href="/wiki/United_States_federal_courts" title="United States federal courts">federal court</a> challenge to California's <a href="/wiki/Zero-emissions_vehicle" title="Zero-emissions vehicle">zero-emissions vehicle</a> mandate, 2) a federal regulation requiring GM to produce and maintain spare parts for the few thousands EV1s and 3) the success of the oil and auto industries' media campaign to reduce public acceptance of EVs.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:EV1A014_(1)_cropped.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/EV1A014_%281%29_cropped.jpg/220px-EV1A014_%281%29_cropped.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/EV1A014_%281%29_cropped.jpg/330px-EV1A014_%281%29_cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/EV1A014_%281%29_cropped.jpg/440px-EV1A014_%281%29_cropped.jpg 2x" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:EV1A014_(1)_cropped.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf13/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/General_Motors_EV1" title="General Motors EV1">General Motors EV1</a> electric car</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>A movie made on the subject in 2005-2006 was titled <i><a href="/wiki/Who_Killed_the_Electric_Car%3F" title="Who Killed the Electric Car?">Who Killed the Electric Car?</a></i> and released theatrically by <a href="/wiki/Sony_Pictures_Classics" title="Sony Pictures Classics">Sony Pictures Classics</a> in 2006. The film explores the roles of <a href="/wiki/Automobile_manufacturer" title="Automobile manufacturer" class="mw-redirect">automobile manufacturers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oil_industry" title="Oil industry" class="mw-redirect">oil industry</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Federal_government_of_the_United_States" title="Federal government of the United States">U.S. government</a>, <a href="/wiki/Battery_(electricity)" title="Battery (electricity)">batteries</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen_(car)" title="Hydrogen (car)" class="mw-redirect">hydrogen vehicles</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Consumer" title="Consumer">consumers</a>, and each of their roles in limiting the deployment and adoption of this technology.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Ford" title="Ford" class="mw-redirect">Ford</a> released a number of their <a href="/wiki/Ford_Ecostar" title="Ford Ecostar">Ford Ecostar</a> delivery vans into the market. Honda, Nissan and Toyota also repossessed and crushed most of their EVs, which, like the GM EV1s, had been available only by closed-end lease. After public protests, Toyota sold 200 of its <a href="/wiki/Toyota_RAV4_EV" title="Toyota RAV4 EV">RAV EVs</a> to eager buyers; they now sell, five years later, at over their original forty-thousand-dollar price. This lesson did not go unlearned; <a href="/wiki/BMW" title="BMW">BMW</a> of Canada sold off a number of Mini EV's when their Canadian testing ended.</p>
<p>The production of the <a href="/wiki/Citro%C3%ABn_Berlingo_Electrique" title="Citroën Berlingo Electrique" class="mw-redirect">Citroën Berlingo Electrique</a> stopped in September 2005.<br style="clear:both;" /></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Reintroduction">Reintroduction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Reintroduction">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Reintroduction" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tesla.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Tesla.jpg/220px-Tesla.jpg" width="220" height="122" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Tesla.jpg/330px-Tesla.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Tesla.jpg/440px-Tesla.jpg 2x" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tesla.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf13/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>
A <a href="/wiki/Tesla_Roadster" title="Tesla Roadster">Tesla Roadster</a>, a <a href="/wiki/REVAi" title="REVAi">REVAi</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Th!nk_City" title="Th!nk City" class="mw-redirect">Th!nk City</a> at a free parking and charging station in Oslo, Norway. The country has the largest electric car ownership per capita in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-NorwayLargest_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NorwayLargest-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Prius" title="Toyota Prius">Toyota Prius</a>, the first mass-produced <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_electric_vehicle" title="Hybrid electric vehicle">hybrid gasoline-electric car</a>, was introduced worldwide in 2001. As of March 2013<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, a total of 2.93&#160;million Prius cars have been sold worldwide in three generations, and it is the world's best selling hybrid.<sup id="cite_ref-TMC5miHEVs_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TMC5miHEVs-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> As of June 2013<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, <a href="/wiki/Series_production" title="Series production" class="mw-redirect">series production</a> <a href="/wiki/All-electric_car" title="All-electric car" class="mw-redirect">all-electric cars</a> available in some countries include the <a href="/wiki/REVAi" title="REVAi">REVAi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buddy_(electric_car)" title="Buddy (electric car)">Buddy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mitsubishi_i_MiEV" title="Mitsubishi i MiEV" class="mw-redirect">Mitsubishi i MiEV</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chery_QQ3_EV" title="Chery QQ3 EV" class="mw-redirect">Chery QQ3 EV</a>, <a href="/wiki/JAC_J3_EV" title="JAC J3 EV" class="mw-redirect">JAC J3 EV</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nissan_Leaf" title="Nissan Leaf">Nissan Leaf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Smart_ED" title="Smart ED" class="mw-redirect">Smart ED</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wheego_Whip_LiFe" title="Wheego Whip LiFe" class="mw-redirect">Wheego Whip LiFe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mia_electric" title="Mia electric">Mia electric</a>, <a href="/wiki/BYD_e6" title="BYD e6">BYD e6</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bollor%C3%A9_Bluecar" title="Bolloré Bluecar">Bolloré Bluecar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Renault_Fluence_Z.E." title="Renault Fluence Z.E.">Renault Fluence Z.E.</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ford_Focus_Electric" title="Ford Focus Electric">Ford Focus Electric</a>, <a href="/wiki/BMW_ActiveE" title="BMW ActiveE">BMW ActiveE</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tesla_Model_S" title="Tesla Model S">Tesla Model S</a>, <a href="/wiki/Honda_Fit_EV" title="Honda Fit EV" class="mw-redirect">Honda Fit EV</a>, <a href="/wiki/Toyota_RAV4_EV_Concept" title="Toyota RAV4 EV Concept" class="mw-redirect">RAV4 EV second generation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Renault_Zoe" title="Renault Zoe">Renault Zoe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roewe_E50" title="Roewe E50" class="mw-redirect">Roewe E50</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mahindra_e2o" title="Mahindra e2o">Mahindra e2o</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet_Spark_EV" title="Chevrolet Spark EV" class="mw-redirect">Chevrolet Spark EV</a>. The Leaf, with more than 65,000 units sold worldwide through May 2013, is the world's top-selling highway-capable all-electric car in history.<sup id="cite_ref-Leaf65K_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Leaf65K-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>As of June 2013<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, production <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_hybrid" title="Plug-in hybrid">plug-in hybrids</a> available include the <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet_Volt" title="Chevrolet Volt">Chevrolet Volt</a>/Opel Ampera, <a href="/wiki/Fisker_Karma" title="Fisker Karma">Fisker Karma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Prius_Plug-in_Hybrid" title="Toyota Prius Plug-in Hybrid">Toyota Prius Plug-in Hybrid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ford_C-Max_Energi" title="Ford C-Max Energi" class="mw-redirect">Ford C-Max Energi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Volvo_V60_Plug-in_Hybrid" title="Volvo V60 Plug-in Hybrid" class="mw-redirect">Volvo V60 Plug-in Hybrid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Honda_Accord_Plug-in_Hybrid" title="Honda Accord Plug-in Hybrid" class="mw-redirect">Honda Accord Plug-in Hybrid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mitsubishi_Outlander_P-HEV" title="Mitsubishi Outlander P-HEV" class="mw-redirect">Mitsubishi Outlander P-HEV</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ford_Fusion_Energi" title="Ford Fusion Energi" class="mw-redirect">Ford Fusion Energi</a>. The Chevrolet Volt family, with more than 45,000 units sold through April 2013 in the U.S., Canada, the Netherlands, Germany, and other European countries, is the world’s best-selling plug-in hybrid.<sup id="cite_ref-PEVsalesUS0612_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PEVsalesUS0612-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PEVsalesUS0512_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PEVsalesUS0512-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NetherSales2012_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NetherSales2012-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SalesGer2011_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SalesGer2011-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SalesGer2012_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SalesGer2012-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-VoltSalesCan_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VoltSalesCan-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SalesSwiss11_12_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SalesSwiss11_12-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Electricity_sources">Electricity sources</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Electricity sources">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Electricity sources" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2402_%27County_of_Hampshire%27_at_Wool.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/2402_%27County_of_Hampshire%27_at_Wool.JPG/220px-2402_%27County_of_Hampshire%27_at_Wool.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/2402_%27County_of_Hampshire%27_at_Wool.JPG/330px-2402_%27County_of_Hampshire%27_at_Wool.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/2402_%27County_of_Hampshire%27_at_Wool.JPG/440px-2402_%27County_of_Hampshire%27_at_Wool.JPG 2x" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2402_%27County_of_Hampshire%27_at_Wool.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf13/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>
A passenger train, taking power through a <a href="/wiki/Third_rail" title="Third rail">third rail</a> with return through the traction rails</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:SwissMGB.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/14/SwissMGB.jpg/220px-SwissMGB.jpg" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/14/SwissMGB.jpg/330px-SwissMGB.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/14/SwissMGB.jpg/440px-SwissMGB.jpg 2x" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:SwissMGB.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf13/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>
An electric Locomotive at <a href="/wiki/Brig,_Switzerland" title="Brig, Switzerland" class="mw-redirect">Brig, Switzerland</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>There are many ways to generate electricity, of varying costs, efficiency and ecological desirability.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Connection_to_generator_plants">Connection to generator plants</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Connection to generator plants">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Connection to generator plants" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>direct connection to generation plants as is common among <a href="/wiki/Electric_train" title="Electric train">electric trains</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trolleybus" title="Trolleybus">trolley buses</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Trolleytruck" title="Trolleytruck">trolley trucks</a> (See also&#160;: <a href="/wiki/Overhead_lines" title="Overhead lines" class="mw-redirect">overhead lines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Third_rail" title="Third rail">third rail</a> and <a href="/wiki/Conduit_current_collection" title="Conduit current collection">conduit current collection</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Online_Electric_Vehicle" title="Online Electric Vehicle">Online Electric Vehicle</a> collects power from electric power strips buried under the road surface through <a href="/wiki/Electromagnetic_induction" title="Electromagnetic induction">electromagnetic induction</a></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Onboard_generators_and_hybrid_EVs">Onboard generators and hybrid EVs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Onboard generators and hybrid EVs">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Onboard generators and hybrid EVs" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>(See articles on <a href="/wiki/Diesel-electric_transmission" title="Diesel-electric transmission">diesel-electric</a> and gasoline-electric <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_vehicle" title="Hybrid vehicle">hybrid</a> locomotion for information on EVs using also <a href="/wiki/Internal_combustion_engine" title="Internal combustion engine">combustion engines</a>).</p>
<ul>
<li>renewable sources such as <a href="/wiki/Solar_power" title="Solar power">solar power</a>: <a href="/wiki/Solar_vehicle" title="Solar vehicle">solar vehicle</a></li>
<li>generated on-board using a diesel engine: <a href="/wiki/Diesel-electric_transmission" title="Diesel-electric transmission">diesel-electric</a> locomotive</li>
<li>generated on-board using a <a href="/wiki/Fuel_cell" title="Fuel cell">fuel cell</a>: <a href="/wiki/Fuel_cell_vehicle" title="Fuel cell vehicle">fuel cell vehicle</a></li>
<li>generated on-board using <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power" title="Nuclear power">nuclear energy</a>: nuclear <a href="/wiki/Submarine" title="Submarine">submarines</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_carrier" title="Aircraft carrier">aircraft carriers</a></li>
</ul>
<p>It is also possible to have hybrid EVs that derive electricity from multiple sources. Such as:</p>
<ul>
<li>on-board <a href="/wiki/Rechargeable_electricity_storage_system" title="Rechargeable electricity storage system" class="mw-redirect">rechargeable electricity storage system</a> (RESS) and a direct continuous connection to land-based generation plants for purposes of on-highway recharging with unrestricted highway range</li>
<li>on-board rechargeable electricity storage system and a fueled propulsion power source (<a href="/wiki/Internal_combustion_engine" title="Internal combustion engine">internal combustion engine</a>): <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_hybrid" title="Plug-in hybrid">plug-in hybrid</a></li>
</ul>
<p>Another form of chemical to electrical conversion is <a href="/wiki/Fuel_cell" title="Fuel cell">fuel cells</a>, projected for future use.</p>
<p>For especially large EVs, such as <a href="/wiki/Submarine" title="Submarine">submarines</a>, the chemical energy of the diesel-electric can be replaced by a <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_reactor" title="Nuclear reactor">nuclear reactor</a>. The nuclear reactor usually provides heat, which drives a <a href="/wiki/Steam_turbine" title="Steam turbine">steam turbine</a>, which drives a generator, which is then fed to the propulsion. <i>See <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_Power" title="Nuclear Power" class="mw-redirect">Nuclear Power</a></i></p>
<p>A few experimental vehicles, such as some cars and a handful of aircraft use <a href="/wiki/Solar_panel" title="Solar panel">solar panels</a> for electricity.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Onboard_storage">Onboard storage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Onboard storage">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Onboard storage" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>These systems are powered from an external generator plant (nearly always when stationary), and then disconnected before motion occurs, and the electricity is stored in the vehicle until needed.</p>
<ul>
<li>on-board <a href="/wiki/Rechargeable_electricity_storage_system" title="Rechargeable electricity storage system" class="mw-redirect">rechargeable electricity storage system</a> (RESS), called Full Electric Vehicles (FEV). Power storage methods include:
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Chemical_energy" title="Chemical energy">chemical energy</a> stored on the vehicle in on-board batteries: <a href="/wiki/Battery_electric_vehicle" title="Battery electric vehicle">Battery electric vehicle</a> (BEV)</li>
<li>static <a href="/wiki/Energy" title="Energy">energy</a> stored on the vehicle in on-board <a href="/wiki/Electric_double-layer_capacitor" title="Electric double-layer capacitor">electric double-layer capacitors</a></li>
<li>kinetic energy storage: <a href="/wiki/Gyrobus" title="Gyrobus">flywheels</a></li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<p><a href="/wiki/Battery_(electricity)" title="Battery (electricity)">Batteries</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electric_double-layer_capacitor" title="Electric double-layer capacitor">electric double-layer capacitors</a> and <a href="/wiki/Flywheel_energy_storage" title="Flywheel energy storage">flywheel energy storage</a> are forms of rechargeable on-board <a href="/wiki/Rechargeable_electricity_storage_system" title="Rechargeable electricity storage system" class="mw-redirect">electrical storage</a>. By avoiding an intermediate mechanical step, the <a href="/wiki/Energy_conversion_efficiency" title="Energy conversion efficiency">energy conversion efficiency</a> can be improved over the hybrids already discussed, by avoiding unnecessary energy conversions. Furthermore, electro-chemical batteries conversions are easy to reverse, allowing electrical energy to be stored in chemical form.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Electric_motor">Electric motor</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Electric motor">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Electric motor" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Traction_motor" title="Traction motor">Traction motor</a> and <a href="/wiki/Energy_conversion_efficiency" title="Energy conversion efficiency">Energy conversion efficiency</a></div>
<p>The power of a vehicle electric motor, as in other vehicles, is measured in <a href="/wiki/Kilowatt" title="Kilowatt" class="mw-redirect">kilowatts</a> (kW). 100&#160;kW is roughly equivalent to 134 <a href="/wiki/Horsepower" title="Horsepower">horsepower</a>, although most electric motors deliver full torque over a wide RPM range, so the performance is not equivalent, and far exceeds a 134 horsepower (100&#160;kW) fuel-powered motor, which has a limited torque curve.<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Usually, <a href="/wiki/Direct_current" title="Direct current">direct current</a> (DC) electricity is fed into a DC/AC inverter where it is converted to <a href="/wiki/Alternating_current" title="Alternating current">alternating current</a> (AC) electricity and this AC electricity is connected to a 3-phase AC motor. For electric trains, DC motors are often used.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Vehicle_types">Vehicle types</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Vehicle types">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Vehicle types" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>It is generally possible to equip any kind of vehicle with an electric powertrain.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Plug-in_electric_vehicle">Plug-in electric vehicle</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Plug-in electric vehicle">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Plug-in electric vehicle" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_electric_vehicle" title="Plug-in electric vehicle">Plug-in electric vehicle</a></div>
<p>A plug-in electric vehicle (PEV) is any <a href="/wiki/Motor_vehicle" title="Motor vehicle">motor vehicle</a> that can be recharged from any external source of electricity, such as <a href="/wiki/Wall_socket" title="Wall socket" class="mw-redirect">wall sockets</a>, and the electricity stored in the <a href="/wiki/Rechargeable_battery" title="Rechargeable battery">rechargeable battery packs</a> drives or contributes to drive the wheels. PEV is a subcategory of electric vehicles that includes <a href="/wiki/All-electric_vehicle" title="All-electric vehicle" class="mw-redirect">all-electric or battery electric vehicles</a> (BEVs), <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_hybrid_vehicle" title="Plug-in hybrid vehicle" class="mw-redirect">plug-in hybrid vehicles</a>, (PHEVs), and <a href="/wiki/Electric_vehicle_conversion" title="Electric vehicle conversion">electric vehicle conversions</a> of <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_electric_vehicle" title="Hybrid electric vehicle">hybrid electric vehicles</a> and conventional <a href="/wiki/Internal_combustion_engine" title="Internal combustion engine">internal combustion engine</a> vehicles.<sup id="cite_ref-PEVs_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PEVs-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CSE_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CSE-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hybrid_EVs">Hybrid EVs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Hybrid EVs">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Hybrid EVs" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_electric_vehicle" title="Hybrid electric vehicle">Hybrid electric vehicle</a> and <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_hybrid" title="Plug-in hybrid">Plug-in hybrid</a></div>
<p>A hybrid EV combines a conventional (usually fossil fuel-powered) powertrain with some form of electric propulsion. Common examples include hybrid electric cars such as the <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Prius" title="Toyota Prius">Toyota Prius</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet_Volt" title="Chevrolet Volt">Chevrolet Volt</a> is an example of a production <a href="/w/index.php?title=Extended_Range_Plug-In_Electric_Vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Extended Range Plug-In Electric Vehicle (page does not exist)">Extended Range Plug-In Electric Vehicle</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="On-_and_off-road_EVs">On- and off-road EVs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: On- and off-road EVs">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: On- and off-road EVs" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Electric_powertrain.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Electric_powertrain.jpg/220px-Electric_powertrain.jpg" width="220" height="85" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Electric_powertrain.jpg/330px-Electric_powertrain.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/c2/Electric_powertrain.jpg 2x" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Electric_powertrain.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf13/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>
An electric powertrain used by <a href="/wiki/Power_Vehicle_Innovation" title="Power Vehicle Innovation">Power Vehicle Innovation</a> for <a href="/wiki/Truck" title="Truck">trucks</a> or <a href="/wiki/Bus" title="Bus">buses</a><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>EVs are on the road in many functions, including <a href="/wiki/Electric_cars" title="Electric cars" class="mw-redirect">electric cars</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trolleybus" title="Trolleybus">electric trolleybuses</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electric_bus" title="Electric bus">electric buses</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electric_truck" title="Electric truck">electric trucks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Motorized_bicycle#Electric" title="Motorized bicycle">electric bicycles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electric_motorcycles_and_scooters" title="Electric motorcycles and scooters">electric motorcycles and scooters</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neighborhood_electric_vehicles" title="Neighborhood electric vehicles" class="mw-redirect">neighborhood electric vehicles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Golf_cart" title="Golf cart">golf carts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Milk_float" title="Milk float">milk floats</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Forklift_truck" title="Forklift truck">forklifts</a>. <a href="/wiki/Off-road_vehicle" title="Off-road vehicle">Off-road vehicles</a> include electrified <a href="/wiki/All-terrain_vehicle" title="All-terrain vehicle">all-terrain vehicles</a> and <a href="/wiki/Elec-Trak" title="Elec-Trak">tractors</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Railborne_EVs">Railborne EVs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Railborne EVs">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Railborne EVs" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Railway_electrification_system" title="Railway electrification system">Railway electrification system</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2001-03-31.H-TW2000-Vahrenwalder-Platz.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/2001-03-31.H-TW2000-Vahrenwalder-Platz.jpg/200px-2001-03-31.H-TW2000-Vahrenwalder-Platz.jpg" width="200" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/2001-03-31.H-TW2000-Vahrenwalder-Platz.jpg/300px-2001-03-31.H-TW2000-Vahrenwalder-Platz.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/2001-03-31.H-TW2000-Vahrenwalder-Platz.jpg/400px-2001-03-31.H-TW2000-Vahrenwalder-Platz.jpg 2x" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2001-03-31.H-TW2000-Vahrenwalder-Platz.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf13/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>
A <a href="/wiki/Streetcar" title="Streetcar" class="mw-redirect">streetcar</a> (or <a href="/wiki/Tram" title="Tram">Tram</a>) drawing current from a single overhead wire through a <a href="/wiki/Pantograph_(rail)" title="Pantograph (rail)">pantograph</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The fixed nature of a rail line makes it relatively easy to power EVs through permanent <a href="/wiki/Overhead_lines" title="Overhead lines" class="mw-redirect">overhead lines</a> or electrified <a href="/wiki/Third_rail" title="Third rail">third rails</a>, eliminating the need for heavy onboard batteries. <a href="/wiki/Electric_locomotive" title="Electric locomotive">Electric locomotives</a>, electric <a href="/wiki/Tram" title="Tram">trams/streetcars/trolleys</a>, electric <a href="/wiki/Light_rail_system" title="Light rail system" class="mw-redirect">light rail systems</a>, and electric <a href="/wiki/Rapid_transit" title="Rapid transit">rapid transit</a> are all in common use today, especially in Europe and Asia.</p>
<p>Since electric trains do not need to carry a heavy internal combustion engine or large batteries, they can have very good <a href="/wiki/Power-to-weight_ratio" title="Power-to-weight ratio">power-to-weight ratios</a>. This allows <a href="/wiki/High_speed_train" title="High speed train" class="mw-redirect">high speed trains</a> such as France's double-deck <a href="/wiki/TGV" title="TGV">TGVs</a> to operate at speeds of 320&#160;km/h (200&#160;mph) or higher, and <a href="/wiki/Electric_locomotive" title="Electric locomotive">electric locomotives</a> to have a much higher power output than <a href="/wiki/Diesel_locomotive" title="Diesel locomotive">diesel locomotives</a>. In addition they have higher short-term <a href="/wiki/Overcurrent" title="Overcurrent">surge power</a> for fast acceleration, and using <a href="/wiki/Regenerative_braking" title="Regenerative braking" class="mw-redirect">regenerative braking</a> can put braking power back into the <a href="/wiki/Electrical_grid" title="Electrical grid">electrical grid</a> rather than wasting it.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Maglev_(transport)" title="Maglev (transport)" class="mw-redirect">Maglev</a> trains are also nearly always EVs.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Airborne_EVs">Airborne EVs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Airborne EVs">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Airborne EVs" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Since the beginning of the era of <a href="/wiki/Aviation" title="Aviation">aviation</a>, electric power for aircraft has received a great deal of experimentation. Currently flying <a href="/wiki/Electric_aircraft" title="Electric aircraft">electric aircraft</a> include manned and unmanned aerial vehicles.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Seaborne_EVs">Seaborne EVs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Seaborne EVs">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Seaborne EVs" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="rellink boilerplate seealso">See also: <a href="/wiki/Submarine#Propulsion" title="Submarine">Submarine#Propulsion</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ship#Propulsion_systems" title="Ship">Ship#Propulsion_systems</a>,&#160;and <a href="/wiki/Electric_boat" title="Electric boat">electric boat</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Oceanvolt_sd8.6_electric_saildrive_motor.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Oceanvolt_sd8.6_electric_saildrive_motor.jpg/220px-Oceanvolt_sd8.6_electric_saildrive_motor.jpg" width="220" height="315" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Oceanvolt_sd8.6_electric_saildrive_motor.jpg/330px-Oceanvolt_sd8.6_electric_saildrive_motor.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/08/Oceanvolt_sd8.6_electric_saildrive_motor.jpg 2x" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Oceanvolt_sd8.6_electric_saildrive_motor.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf13/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>
Oceanvolt SD8.6 electric saildrive motor</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Electric_boat" title="Electric boat">Electric boats</a> were popular around the turn of the 20th century. Interest in quiet and potentially renewable marine transportation has steadily increased since the late 20th century, as <a href="/wiki/Solar_cells" title="Solar cells" class="mw-redirect">solar cells</a> have given <a href="/wiki/Motorboat" title="Motorboat">motorboats</a> the infinite range of <a href="/wiki/Sailboats" title="Sailboats" class="mw-redirect">sailboats</a>. Electric motors can and have also been used in sailboats instead of traditional diesel engines.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Submarine" title="Submarine">Submarines</a> use batteries (charged by <a href="/wiki/Diesel-electric_transmission" title="Diesel-electric transmission">diesel</a> or gasoline engines at the surface), <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_submarine" title="Nuclear submarine">nuclear</a> power, fuel cells<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> or <a href="/wiki/Stirling_engine" title="Stirling engine">Stirling engines</a> to run electric motor-driven propellers.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Spaceborne_EVs">Spaceborne EVs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Spaceborne EVs">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Spaceborne EVs" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Electrically_powered_spacecraft_propulsion" title="Electrically powered spacecraft propulsion">Electrically powered spacecraft propulsion</a></div>
<p>Electric power has a long history of use in <a href="/wiki/Spacecraft" title="Spacecraft">spacecraft</a>. The power sources used for spacecraft are batteries, solar panels and nuclear power. Current methods of propelling a spacecraft with electricity include the <a href="/wiki/Arcjet_rocket" title="Arcjet rocket">arcjet rocket</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Electrostatic_ion_thruster" title="Electrostatic ion thruster">electrostatic ion thruster</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Hall_effect_thruster" title="Hall effect thruster">Hall effect thruster</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Field_Emission_Electric_Propulsion" title="Field Emission Electric Propulsion" class="mw-redirect">Field Emission Electric Propulsion</a>. <a href="/wiki/Spacecraft_propulsion#Table_of_methods" title="Spacecraft propulsion">A number of other methods have been proposed, with varying levels of feasibility</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy_and_motors">Energy and motors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Energy and motors">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Energy and motors" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tr%C3%A5dbuss_Landskrona.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Tr%C3%A5dbuss_Landskrona.JPG/220px-Tr%C3%A5dbuss_Landskrona.JPG" width="220" height="160" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Tr%C3%A5dbuss_Landskrona.JPG/330px-Tr%C3%A5dbuss_Landskrona.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Tr%C3%A5dbuss_Landskrona.JPG/440px-Tr%C3%A5dbuss_Landskrona.JPG 2x" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tr%C3%A5dbuss_Landskrona.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf13/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>
A <a href="/wiki/Trolleybus" title="Trolleybus">trolleybus</a> uses two overhead wires to provide electric current supply and return to the power source</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:SwissElectricBus.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/SwissElectricBus.jpg/220px-SwissElectricBus.jpg" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/SwissElectricBus.jpg/330px-SwissElectricBus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/SwissElectricBus.jpg/440px-SwissElectricBus.jpg 2x" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:SwissElectricBus.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf13/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>
An electric bus at <a href="/wiki/Lucerne" title="Lucerne">Lucerne</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Most large electric transport systems are powered by stationary sources of electricity that are directly connected to the vehicles through wires. Electric traction allows the use of <a href="/wiki/Regenerative_braking" title="Regenerative braking" class="mw-redirect">regenerative braking</a>, in which the motors are used as brakes and become generators that transform the motion of, usually, a train into electrical power that is then fed back into the lines. This system is particularly advantageous in mountainous operations, as descending vehicles can produce a large portion of the power required for those ascending. This regenerative system is only viable if the system is large enough to utilise the power generated by descending vehicles.</p>
<p>In the systems above motion is provided by a <a href="/wiki/Rotary_motor" title="Rotary motor" class="mw-redirect">rotary</a> <a href="/wiki/Electric_motor" title="Electric motor">electric motor</a>. However, it is possible to "unroll" the motor to drive directly against a special matched track. These <a href="/wiki/Linear_motor" title="Linear motor">linear motors</a> are used in <a href="/wiki/Maglev_train" title="Maglev train" class="mw-redirect">maglev trains</a> which float above the rails supported by <a href="/wiki/Magnetic_levitation" title="Magnetic levitation">magnetic levitation</a>. This allows for almost no rolling resistance of the vehicle and no mechanical wear and tear of the train or track. In addition to the high-performance control systems needed, <a href="/wiki/Railroad_switch" title="Railroad switch">switching</a> and curving of the tracks becomes difficult with linear motors, which to date has restricted their operations to high-speed point to point services.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Properties_of_EVs">Properties of EVs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Properties of EVs">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Properties of EVs" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Components">Components</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Components">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Components" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The type of <a href="/wiki/Electric_vehicle_battery" title="Electric vehicle battery">battery</a>, the type of <a href="/wiki/Traction_motor" title="Traction motor">traction motor</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Motor_controller" title="Motor controller">motor controller</a> design vary according to the size, power and proposed application, which can be as small as a <a href="/wiki/Motorized_shopping_cart" title="Motorized shopping cart">motorized shopping cart</a> or <a href="/wiki/Wheelchair" title="Wheelchair">wheelchair</a>, through <a href="/wiki/Pedelec" title="Pedelec">pedelecs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electric_motorcycles_and_scooters" title="Electric motorcycles and scooters">electric motorcycles and scooters</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neighborhood_electric_vehicles" title="Neighborhood electric vehicles" class="mw-redirect">neighborhood electric vehicles</a>, industrial <a href="/wiki/Fork-lift_truck" title="Fork-lift truck" class="mw-redirect">fork-lift trucks</a> and including many <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_vehicle" title="Hybrid vehicle">hybrid vehicles</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy_sources">Energy sources</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Energy sources">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Energy sources" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Although EVs have few direct emissions, all rely on energy created through <a href="/wiki/Electricity_generation" title="Electricity generation">electricity generation</a>, and will usually emit pollution and generate waste, unless it is generated by <a href="/wiki/Renewable_source" title="Renewable source" class="mw-redirect">renewable source</a> power plants. Since EVs use whatever electricity is delivered by their electrical utility/grid operator, EVs can be made more or less efficient, polluting and expensive to run, by modifying the electrical generating stations. This would be done by an electrical utility under a government energy policy, in a timescale negotiated between utilities and government.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel" title="Fossil fuel">Fossil fuel</a> vehicle efficiency and pollution standards take years to filter through a nation's fleet of vehicles. New efficiency and pollution standards rely on the purchase of new vehicles, often as the current vehicles already on the road reach their end-of-life. Only a few nations set a retirement age for old vehicles, such as Japan or <a href="/wiki/Driving_in_Singapore" title="Driving in Singapore">Singapore</a>, forcing periodic upgrading of all vehicles already on the road.</p>
<p>EVs will take advantage of whatever environmental gains happen when a renewable energy generation station comes online, a <a href="/wiki/Fossil-fuel_power_station" title="Fossil-fuel power station">fossil-fuel power station</a> is decommissioned or upgraded. Conversely, if government policy or economic conditions shifts generators back to use more polluting fossil fuels and <a href="/wiki/Internal_combustion_engine_vehicle" title="Internal combustion engine vehicle" class="mw-redirect">internal combustion engine vehicles</a> (ICEVs), or more inefficient sources, the reverse can happen. Even in such a situation, electrical vehicles are still more efficient than a comparable amount of fossil fuel vehicles. In areas with a deregulated electrical energy market, an electrical vehicle owner can choose whether to run his electrical vehicle off conventional electrical energy sources, or strictly from renewable electrical energy sources (presumably at an additional cost), pushing other consumers onto conventional sources, and switch at any time between the two.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Issues_with_batteries">Issues with batteries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Issues with batteries">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Issues with batteries" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Electric_vehicle_battery" title="Electric vehicle battery">Electric vehicle battery</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Photo-CarBattery.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Photo-CarBattery.jpg/220px-Photo-CarBattery.jpg" width="220" height="210" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Photo-CarBattery.jpg/330px-Photo-CarBattery.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Photo-CarBattery.jpg/440px-Photo-CarBattery.jpg 2x" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Photo-CarBattery.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf13/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>
Old: Banks of conventional lead-acid car batteries are still commonly used for EV propulsion</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:NASA_Lithium_Ion_Polymer_Battery.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/NASA_Lithium_Ion_Polymer_Battery.jpg/220px-NASA_Lithium_Ion_Polymer_Battery.jpg" width="220" height="194" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/NASA_Lithium_Ion_Polymer_Battery.jpg/330px-NASA_Lithium_Ion_Polymer_Battery.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b7/NASA_Lithium_Ion_Polymer_Battery.jpg 2x" /></a>

75&#160;watt-hour/kilogram <a href="/wiki/Lithium_ion_polymer_battery" title="Lithium ion polymer battery" class="mw-redirect">lithium ion polymer battery</a> prototypes. Newer Li-poly cells provide up to 130 Wh/kg and last through thousands of charging cycles.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Efficiency">Efficiency</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Efficiency">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Efficiency" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Because of the different methods of charging possible, the emissions produced have been quantified in different ways.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> Plug-in all-electric and hybrid vehicles also have different consumption characteristics.<sup id="cite_ref-knipping_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-knipping-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Electromagnetic_radiation">Electromagnetic radiation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Electromagnetic radiation">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Electromagnetic radiation" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Electromagnetic_radiation" title="Electromagnetic radiation">Electromagnetic radiation</a> from high performance electrical motors has been claimed to be associated with some human ailments, but such claims are largely unsubstantiated except for extremely high exposures.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> Electric motors can be shielded within a metallic <a href="/wiki/Faraday_cage" title="Faraday cage">Faraday cage</a>, but this reduces efficiency by adding weight to the vehicle, while it is not conclusive that all electromagnetic radiation can be contained.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Charging">Charging</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Charging">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Charging" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Grid_capacity">Grid capacity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Grid capacity">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Grid capacity" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>If a large proportion of private vehicles were to convert to grid electricity it would increase the demand for generation and transmission, and consequent emissions. However, overall energy consumption and emissions would diminish because of the higher efficiency of EVs over the entire cycle. In the USA it has been estimated there is already nearly sufficient existing power plant and transmission infrastructure, assuming that most charging would occur overnight, using the most efficient off-peak <a href="/wiki/Base_load" title="Base load" class="mw-redirect">base load</a> sources.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In the UK however, things are different. While National Grid’s high-voltage electricity transmission system can currently manage the demand of 1 million electric cars, Steve Holliday (CEO National Grid PLC) said, “penetration up and above that becomes a real issue. Local distribution networks in cities like London may struggle to balance their grids if drivers choose to all plug in their cars at the same time."</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Charging_stations">Charging stations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Charging stations">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Charging stations" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Charging_station" title="Charging station">Charging station</a></div>
<p>EVs typically charge from conventional power outlets or dedicated charging stations, a process that typically takes hours, but can be done overnight and often gives a charge that is sufficient for normal everyday usage.</p>
<p>However with the widespread implementation of <a href="/wiki/Electric_vehicle_network" title="Electric vehicle network">electric vehicle networks</a> within large cities, such as those provided by POD Point <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.pod-point.com/">[3]</a> in the UK and Europe, EV users can plug in their cars whilst at work and leave them to charge throughout the day, extending the possible range of commutes and eliminating <a href="/wiki/Range_anxiety" title="Range anxiety">range anxiety</a>.</p>
<p>A recharging system that avoids the need for a cable is <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.ridek.com/Curb_Connect/Curb_Connect.htm">Curb Connect</a>, patented in 2012<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> by Dr Gordon Dower. In this system, electrical contacts are fitting into curbs, such as angle parking spaces on city streets. When a suitably authorized vehicle is parked so that its front end overhangs the curb, the curb contacts become energized and charging occurs.</p>
<p>Another proposed solution for daily recharging is a standardized <a href="/wiki/Inductive_charging" title="Inductive charging">inductive charging</a> system such as Evatran's <a href="/wiki/Plugless_Power" title="Plugless Power">Plugless Power</a>. Benefits are the convenience of with parking over the charge station and minimized cabling and connection infrastructure.<sup id="cite_ref-cleantech100120_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cleantech100120-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-swvatoday090918_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-swvatoday090918-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bnet100226_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bnet100226-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Qualcomm" title="Qualcomm">Qualcomm</a> is trialling such a system in London in early 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Yet another proposed solution for the typically less frequent, long distance travel is "rapid charging", such as the <a href="/wiki/Aerovironment" title="Aerovironment" class="mw-redirect">Aerovironment</a> PosiCharge line (up to 250&#160;kW) and the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Norvik&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Norvik (page does not exist)">Norvik</a> MinitCharge line (up to 300&#160;kW). <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ecotality&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ecotality (page does not exist)">Ecotality</a> is a manufacturer of Charging Stations and has partnered with Nissan on several installations. Battery replacement is also proposed as an alternative, although no OEMs including Nissan/Renault have any production vehicle plans. Swapping requires standardization across platforms, models and manufacturers. Swapping also requires many times more battery packs to be in the system.</p>
<p>One type of battery "replacement" proposed, <a href="/wiki/Vanadium_redox_battery" title="Vanadium redox battery">vanadium redox battery</a>, is much simpler: while the latest generation of <a href="/wiki/Vanadium_redox_battery" title="Vanadium redox battery">vanadium redox battery</a> only has an energy density similar to lead-acid, the charge is stored solely in a vanadium-based electrolyte, which can be pumped out and replaced with charged fluid<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>. The vanadium battery system is also a potential candidate for intermediate energy storage in quick charging stations because of its high power density and extremely good endurance in daily use<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>. System cost however, is still prohibitive. As vanadium battery systems are estimated to range between $350–$600 per kWh, a battery that can service one hundred customers in a 24 hour period at 50 kWh per charge would cost $1.8-$3 million<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>.</p>
<p>According to <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Energy" title="United States Department of Energy">Department of Energy</a> research conducted at <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Northwest_National_Laboratory" title="Pacific Northwest National Laboratory">Pacific Northwest National Laboratory</a>, 84% of existing vehicles could be switched over to <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_hybrid" title="Plug-in hybrid">plug-in hybrids</a> without requiring any new grid infrastructure.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup> In terms of transportation, the net result would be a 27% total reduction in emissions of the <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas" title="Greenhouse gas">greenhouse gases</a> <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide">carbon dioxide</a>, <a href="/wiki/Methane" title="Methane">methane</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Nitrous_oxide" title="Nitrous oxide">nitrous oxide</a>, a 31% total reduction in <a href="/wiki/Nitrogen_oxide" title="Nitrogen oxide">nitrogen oxides</a>, a slight reduction in nitrous oxide emissions, an increase in <a href="/wiki/Atmospheric_particulate_matter" title="Atmospheric particulate matter" class="mw-redirect">particulate matter</a> emissions, the same <a href="/wiki/Sulfur_dioxide" title="Sulfur dioxide">sulfur dioxide</a> emissions, and the near elimination of <a href="/wiki/Carbon_monoxide" title="Carbon monoxide">carbon monoxide</a> and <a href="/wiki/Volatile_organic_compound" title="Volatile organic compound">volatile organic compound</a> emissions (a 98% decrease in carbon monoxide and a 93% decrease in volatile organic compounds).<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> The emissions would be displaced away from street level, where they have "high human-health implications."<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Battery_swapping">Battery swapping</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Battery swapping">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Battery swapping" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Instead of recharging EVs from electric socket, batteries could be mechanically replaced on special stations in a couple of minutes (<a href="/wiki/Battery_swapping" title="Battery swapping" class="mw-redirect">battery swapping</a>).</p>
