<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eliica.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Eliica.jpg/220px-Eliica.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Eliica.jpg/330px-Eliica.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Eliica.jpg/440px-Eliica.jpg 2x" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eliica.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf13/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Eliica" title="Eliica">Eliica</a> Battery Electric Car with 370 km/h top speed and 200 km range</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:New_Vehicle_Purchase_Preference.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/New_Vehicle_Purchase_Preference.svg/220px-New_Vehicle_Purchase_Preference.svg.png" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/New_Vehicle_Purchase_Preference.svg/330px-New_Vehicle_Purchase_Preference.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/New_Vehicle_Purchase_Preference.svg/440px-New_Vehicle_Purchase_Preference.svg.png 2x" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:New_Vehicle_Purchase_Preference.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf13/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>
The number of US survey respondents willing to pay $4,000 more for a <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_hybrid_electric_vehicle" title="Plug-in hybrid electric vehicle" class="mw-redirect">plug-in hybrid</a> car increased from 17% in 2005 to 26% in 2006.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Ferdinand Dudenhoeffer, head of the <a href="/wiki/Centre_of_Automotive_Research" title="Centre of Automotive Research" class="mw-redirect">Centre of Automotive Research</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Gelsenkirchen_University_of_Applied_Sciences" title="Gelsenkirchen University of Applied Sciences" class="mw-redirect">Gelsenkirchen University of Applied Sciences</a> in Germany, said that "by 2025, all <a href="/wiki/Automobile" title="Automobile">passenger cars</a> sold in Europe will be electric or hybrid electric".<sup id="cite_ref-euobserver.com_91-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-euobserver.com-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Several <a href="/wiki/Startup_company" title="Startup company">startup</a> companies like <a href="/wiki/Tesla_Motors" title="Tesla Motors">Tesla Motors</a>, <a href="/wiki/Commuter_Cars" title="Commuter Cars">Commuter Cars</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Miles_Electric_Vehicles" title="Miles Electric Vehicles">Miles Electric Vehicles</a> will have powerful battery-EVs available to the public in 2008. Battery and energy storage technology is advancing rapidly. The average distance driven by 80% of citizens per day in a car in the US is about 50 miles (US dept of transport, 1991), which fits easily within the current range of the electric car. This range can be improved by technologies such as <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_hybrid" title="Plug-in hybrid">Plug-in hybrid</a> EVs which are capable of using traditional fuels for unlimited range, rapid charging stations for BEVs, improved energy density batteries, <a href="/wiki/Vanadium_redox_battery" title="Vanadium redox battery">flow batteries</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Battery_swapping" title="Battery swapping" class="mw-redirect">battery swapping</a>.</p>
<p>In 2006 GM began the development of a <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_hybrid" title="Plug-in hybrid">plug-in hybrid</a> that will use a lithium-ion battery. The vehicle, initially known as the iCar, is now called the <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet_Volt" title="Chevrolet Volt">Chevrolet Volt</a>. The basic design was first exhibited January 2007 at the North American International Auto Show. GM is planning to have this EV ready for sale to the public in the latter half of 2010. The car is to have a 40-mile (64&#160;km) range. If the battery capacity falls below 30 percent a small internal combustion engine will kick in to charge the battery on the go. This in effect increases the range of the vehicle, allowing it to be driven until it can be fully charged by plugging it into a standard household AC electrical source. In December 2010 Nissan introduced the Nissan Leaf in Japan and the U.S. The Nissan Leaf is a five-door mid-size hatchback electric car. The U.S. Environmental Protection Agency determined the range to be 117 kilometres (73&#160;mi), with an energy consumption of 765 kJ/km (34 kWh per 100 miles).</p>
<p>Among other awards and recognition, the Nissan Leaf won the 2010 Green Car Vision Award award, the 2011 European Car of the Year award, the 2011 World Car of the Year, and ranks as the most efficient EPA certified vehicle for all fuels ever. The Ford <a href="/wiki/C-MAX" title="C-MAX" class="mw-redirect">C-MAX</a> Energi was launched that year in response to the Leaf and Volt, to be available on the market within a year and estimated to have a 500-mile range.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On October 29, 2007, <a href="/wiki/Shai_Agassi" title="Shai Agassi">Shai Agassi</a> launched <a href="/wiki/Project_Better_Place" title="Project Better Place" class="mw-redirect">Project Better Place</a>, a company focused on building massive scale Electric Recharge Grids as infrastructure supporting the deployment of EVs (including plug-in hybrids) in countries around the world. On January 21, 2008, PBP and the <a href="/wiki/Nissan" title="Nissan" class="mw-redirect">Nissan</a>–<a href="/wiki/Renault" title="Renault">Renault</a> group signed a <a href="/wiki/Memorandum_of_understanding" title="Memorandum of understanding">MOU</a> - PBP will provide the battery recharging and swapping infrastructure and Renault-Nissan will mass-produce the vehicles.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Improved_long_term_energy_storage_and_nano_batteries">Improved long term energy storage and nano batteries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=60" title="Edit section: Improved long term energy storage and nano batteries">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=60" title="Edit section: Improved long term energy storage and nano batteries" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There have been several developments which could bring EVs outside their current fields of application, as scooters, golf cars, neighborhood vehicles, in industrial operational yards and indoor operation. First, advances in <a href="/wiki/Lithium_ion_battery" title="Lithium ion battery" class="mw-redirect">lithium-based battery technology</a>, in large part driven by the consumer electronics industry, allow full-sized, highway-capable EVs to be propelled as far on a single charge as conventional cars go on a single tank of gasoline. Lithium batteries have been made safe, can be recharged in minutes instead of hours, and now last longer than the typical vehicle. The production cost of these lighter, higher-capacity lithium batteries is gradually decreasing as the technology matures and production volumes increase.</p>
<p>Rechargeable <a href="/wiki/Lithium%E2%80%93air_battery" title="Lithium–air battery">lithium-air batteries</a> potentially offer increased range over other types and are a current topic of research.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Introduction_of_battery_management_and_intermediate_storage">Introduction of battery management and intermediate storage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=61" title="Edit section: Introduction of battery management and intermediate storage">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=61" title="Edit section: Introduction of battery management and intermediate storage" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Another improvement is to decouple the electric motor from the battery through electronic control, employing <a href="/wiki/Ultra-capacitor" title="Ultra-capacitor" class="mw-redirect">ultra-capacitors</a> to buffer large but short power demands and <a href="/wiki/Regenerative_braking" title="Regenerative braking" class="mw-redirect">regenerative braking</a> energy. The development of new cell types combined with intelligent cell management improved both weak points mentioned above. The cell management involves not only monitoring the health of the cells but also a redundant cell configuration (one more cell than needed). With sophisticated switched wiring it is possible to condition one cell while the rest are on duty.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Faster_battery_recharging">Faster battery recharging</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=62" title="Edit section: Faster battery recharging">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=62" title="Edit section: Faster battery recharging" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>By soaking the matter found in conventional lithium ion batteries in a special solution, lithium ion batteries were supposedly said to be recharged 100x faster. This test was however done with a specially designed battery with little capacity. Batteries with higher capacity can be recharged 40x faster.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup> The research was conducted by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Byoungwoo_Kang&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Byoungwoo Kang (page does not exist)">Byoungwoo Kang</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gerbrand_Ceder&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Gerbrand Ceder (page does not exist)">Gerbrand Ceder</a> of <a href="/wiki/MIT" title="MIT" class="mw-redirect">MIT</a>. The researchers believe the solution may appear on the market in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup> Another method to speed up battery charging is by adding an additional oscillating electric field. This method was proposed by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ibrahim_Abou_Hamad&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ibrahim Abou Hamad (page does not exist)">Ibrahim Abou Hamad</a> from <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_State_University" title="Mississippi State University">Mississippi State University</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup> In addition, the research done by Junqing Pan, Yanbin Qiu, Yanzhi Sun, and Zihao Wang of <a href="/wiki/Beijing_University_of_Chemical_Technology" title="Beijing University of Chemical Technology">Beijing University of Chemical Technology</a> suggests the possibility of using Silver Cuprate (<a href="/wiki/Chemical_formula" title="Chemical formula">chemical formula</a> AgCuO<sub>2</sub>) to charge batteries, which could make the charging time as fast as refueling the gasoline vehicles.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup> The company <a href="/wiki/Epyon" title="Epyon">Epyon</a> specializes in faster charging of EVs.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Free_Software_EVs">Free Software EVs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=63" title="Edit section: Free Software EVs">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=63" title="Edit section: Free Software EVs" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Tumanako Project aims to provide <a href="/wiki/Open_hardware" title="Open hardware" class="mw-redirect">open hardware</a> and software to drive and recharge EVs.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup> Author Morgen E. Peck covers the project and talks with developer Philip Court. "The main offering of the Tumanako project is a drive package and inverter for a 200kW induction motor. This includes all of the software necessary to take a “go” command from a driver and the calculations for how much power to feed to the motor. Court says his code works but will not be fully open source — meaning there are still snippets of proprietary code — for another 6 months to a year."<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="EV_organizations">EV organizations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=64" title="Edit section: EV organizations">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=64" title="Edit section: EV organizations" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Worldwide">Worldwide</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=65" title="Edit section: Worldwide">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=65" title="Edit section: Worldwide" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <b><a href="/wiki/World_Electric_Vehicle_Association" title="World Electric Vehicle Association">World Electric Vehicle Association</a></b> (WEVA), <a href="/wiki/Chairman" title="Chairman">chairman</a> Hisashi Ishitani, formed by:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Electric_Drive_Transportation_Association" title="Electric Drive Transportation Association" class="mw-redirect">Electric Drive Transportation Association</a> (<a href="/wiki/Electric_Drive_Transportation_Association" title="Electric Drive Transportation Association" class="mw-redirect">EDTA</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Electric_Vehicle_Association_of_Asia_Pacific" title="Electric Vehicle Association of Asia Pacific" class="mw-redirect">Electric Vehicle Association of Asia Pacific</a> (<a href="/wiki/EVAAP" title="EVAAP" class="mw-redirect">EVAAP</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/European_Association_for_Battery,_Hybrid_and_Fuel_Cell_Electric_Vehicles" title="European Association for Battery, Hybrid and Fuel Cell Electric Vehicles" class="mw-redirect">European Association for Battery, Hybrid and Fuel Cell Electric Vehicles</a> (<a href="/wiki/AVERE" title="AVERE" class="mw-redirect">AVERE</a>)</li>
<li><span class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.electricvehiclesresearch.com/">"Electric Vehicles Research"</a>. idtechex.com.</span><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AElectric+vehicle&amp;rft.btitle=Electric+Vehicles+Research&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.electricvehiclesresearch.com%2F&amp;rft.pub=idtechex.com&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></li>
</ul>
<p><b>Multilateral Cooperation to Advance Electric Vehicles</b></p>
<ul>
<li>The Implementing Agreement for co-operation on Hybrid and Electric Vehicle Technologies and Programmes (<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.ieahev.org/"><b>IA-HEV</b></a>)</li>
</ul>
<p>IA-HEV was formed in 1993 to produce and disseminate balanced, objective information about advanced electric, hybrid, and fuel cell vehicles. IA-HEV is an international membership group collaborating under the International Energy Agency (IEA) framework.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="North_America">North America</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=66" title="Edit section: North America">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=66" title="Edit section: North America" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/National_Electric_Drag_Racing_Association" title="National Electric Drag Racing Association">National Electric Drag Racing Association</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Electric_Auto_Association" title="Electric Auto Association">Electric Auto Association</a> (EAA) (North America) and its chapter <a href="/wiki/Plug_In_America" title="Plug In America">Plug In America</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Project_EVIE" title="Project EVIE">Project EVIE</a></li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_Coast_Electric_Drag_Racing_Association&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="East Coast Electric Drag Racing Association (page does not exist)">East Coast Electric Drag Racing Association</a></li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.rawvehicle.com">Magazine About Hybrid Cars And Electric Vehicles</a></li>
</ul>
